  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_00bc676a-9679-4a4b-ac02-a58c17fd4d3b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer2206873208489496367">It's a hot, lazy day, perfect for a cookout, until you see those strange dark clouds. Suddenly a violent storm sweeps across the lake and ends as abruptly and unexpectedly as it had begun. Then comes the mist...creeping slowly, inexorably into town, where it settles and waits, trapping you in the supermarket with dozens of others, cut off from your families and the world. </span>
  <span id="freeText2206873208489496367" style="display:none">It's a hot, lazy day, perfect for a cookout, until you see those strange dark clouds. Suddenly a violent storm sweeps across the lake and ends as abruptly and unexpectedly as it had begun. Then comes the mist...creeping slowly, inexorably into town, where it settles and waits, trapping you in the supermarket with dozens of others, cut off from your families and the world. The mist is alive, seething with unearthly sounds and movements. What unleashed this terror? Was it the Arrowhead Project---the top secret government operation that everyone has noticed but no one quite understands? And what happens when the provisions have run out and you're forced to make your escape, edging blindly through the dim light?</span>
  <a data-text-id="2206873208489496367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2046422449" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2046422449" />
    <a title="Always Pouting" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting"><img alt="Always Pouting" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483476563p2/48650982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2046422449?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Always Pouting" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Always Pouting" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting">Always Pouting</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35155248-the-mist">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2046422449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2678033981646997647">David and his son Billy go out to get grocery store to get supplies after a bad storm has hit town. Before leaving David had noticed a thick mist forming, and started to feel an apprehension building. Figuring it was nothing David and Billy went for supplies but end up sequestered inside the grocery store after someone comes in screaming about the things in the mist. The town is near a military base, where rumor has it nuclear testing is being conducted, and everyone in the store becomes unsure </span>
  <span id="freeText2678033981646997647" style="display:none">David and his son Billy go out to get grocery store to get supplies after a bad storm has hit town. Before leaving David had noticed a thick mist forming, and started to feel an apprehension building. Figuring it was nothing David and Billy went for supplies but end up sequestered inside the grocery store after someone comes in screaming about the things in the mist. The town is near a military base, where rumor has it nuclear testing is being conducted, and everyone in the store becomes unsure about how to proceed. Wondering about whether or not someone is coming to save them, decisions have to be made about the best course of action. <br /><br />I recently read The Thing and hated it but this one went over much better. The suspense was built up much better here and I got pretty on edge waiting to see if they would all make it. I haven't seen any of the TV or movie adaptions of this though so I came in this without any idea about the plot line. I also did like how it left off but someone told me the movie ending is a lot better. I just sometimes feel like Stephen King seems to really take his time when writing and maybe he should try to cut down on the details not related to the scary shit happening which is what I want to read about you know.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2678033981646997647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

King surely knows how to write characters you want to strangle, and then feel happy about it. <br /><br />Even though I really liked the book I need to say one thing. <span id="freeTextContainer15115984077200026323">A very unusual freak storm hits a small Maine town causing a lot of damage. In its aftermath, many of the townsfolk head to the local grocery store to stock up on supplies and food. While there, a thick enveloping heavy mist like no one has ever seen settles around the store. Soon the people discover that something is out there in the mist. But what exactly could it be?<br/><br/>This was an extremely entertaining horror story. I really enjoyed the vivid cast of characters and the different ways they react</span>
  <span id="freeText15115984077200026323" style="display:none">A very unusual freak storm hits a small Maine town causing a lot of damage. In its aftermath, many of the townsfolk head to the local grocery store to stock up on supplies and food. While there, a thick enveloping heavy mist like no one has ever seen settles around the store. Soon the people discover that something is out there in the mist. But what exactly could it be?<br /><br />This was an extremely entertaining horror story. I really enjoyed the vivid cast of characters and the different ways they reacted to their situation while stranded in the store...nerves wearing thin, arguments, choosing sides. The story itself was very atmospheric, with such a sense of foreboding, and I loved the grocery store setting. And what was out there in the mist was pretty wild. Creepy, scary, and a lot of fun. It held my attention throughout.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781982103521" href="/book/show/38926460-the-mist">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/96868145-sandeep?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/96868145-sandeep?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/96868145-sandeep?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2959313250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13766178003501745480"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br/><br/>Just another example of King's mesmerizing storytelling ability. Got me gripped from page 1 until the final sentence. Although being the size of a novella and originally published as a short story, this book has enough to spooke you with all the creeps and chills.<br/><br/>The way King builds up the atmosphere for this is brilliant. The book wastes no time setting itself up and diving into the story, and also doesn’t spend too much time exploring the whys and the whats, it just gets into it all,</span>
  <span id="freeText13766178003501745480" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br /><br />Just another example of King's mesmerizing storytelling ability. Got me gripped from page 1 until the final sentence. Although being the size of a novella and originally published as a short story, this book has enough to spooke you with all the creeps and chills.<br /><br />The way King builds up the atmosphere for this is brilliant. The book wastes no time setting itself up and diving into the story, and also doesn’t spend too much time exploring the whys and the whats, it just gets into it all, which is fantastic.<br /><br />While The Mist is terrifying with its creatures seeking human flesh in the grayness, its real fear comes from the gray of human nature. It revolves around how people react to the terror and each other. That’s the real horror here.<br /><br />My only complain would be that there isn't much explanation about why the mist has suddenly appeared. Also there is a totally unnecessary sex scene in the book. A lot of people don't like the ending, but I quite like it.<br /><br />Overall, The Mist is a pretty damn good short, quick read if you are interested, and has monster horror to keep you going. It knows what it is and it goes for it, no mincing about. It is well written and barrels along, definitely worth the read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13766178003501745480" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3353820978" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3353820978" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3353820978?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3353820978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16782390465167417662">I have always found that Stephen King can pull a reader in with his writing, no matter the length. I needed something to fill my time and turned to this novella, which showcases some of the greatness I have come to expect from the author. David Drayton and his family live in rural Maine, watching as a storm rolls across the sky, closer to them. The fork lightning excites young Billy, who wants to stay up as things seem to be falling apart around him. In the morning, the storm’s destruction is ap</span>
  <span id="freeText16782390465167417662" style="display:none">I have always found that Stephen King can pull a reader in with his writing, no matter the length. I needed something to fill my time and turned to this novella, which showcases some of the greatness I have come to expect from the author. David Drayton and his family live in rural Maine, watching as a storm rolls across the sky, closer to them. The fork lightning excites young Billy, who wants to stay up as things seem to be falling apart around him. In the morning, the storm’s destruction is apparent, with felled power lines and trees having smashed into houses and vehicles alike. David is tasked with getting some things at the store, an activity that he and Billy will do together. However, before they depart, both notice an odd mist hovering over the water, something David can only surmise must be an odd meteorological aberration. As they make their way to town, Billy and David review the list given to them, noticing that the mist seems to be here as well. Once inside, it would seem others had the same idea about grabbing a few things, as David and Billy queue up with other townsfolk. The mist thickens, almost enveloping the store, as many ask about it and what it could mean. Some venture outside, not seen again, but their piercing screams fill the air. Worried now, David and some others try to determine what this mist could be, witnessing a grotesque tentacle emerge and pull someone into its centre. This is no longer a low cloud, but something with a mind of its own. How anyone will get out is left to be seen in this King classic novella. Sharp, with a mix of spine-chilling actions, Stephen King keeps the reader on edge throughout. Recommended to those who enjoy the work of Stephen King, as well as those readers who find pleasure in stories about the weather.<br /><br />I find that Stephen King is able to come up with some many varied ideas in his writing, pulling from his vast experiences. This piece, which begins as a simple nighttime storm, soon becomes a horrifying story about a seemingly innocuous weather system. David Drayton plays the wonderful protagonist in this piece, mixing a laidback nature with a passion to get to the root of the issue. He leads his family in being as safe as possible, but tries to downplay some of the worries his wife exhibits throughout the story. When it comes down to it, David exerts a leadership role that the reader will discover throughout, particularly when things get especially problematic within the store. Other characters offer interesting flavouring to an already hyped-up story, giving King much to work with as he spins this tale effectively. The piece itself is full of wonderful imagery, from the powerful storm to this sinister ‘thing’ floating over the water, which will eventually eject its slimy arms to pull unsuspecting people inside it, as though feeding off the fear that the townspeople have of what’s going on. King never shies away from this detail, which is balanced out by some of the climactic writing that divides the chapters. Anyone looking for some suspenseful work with not too much in the way of gory description need look no further. At a time when some feel they are ‘living in a Stephen King’ novel, I am left to wonder if I would prefer isolation from COVID-19, or from this mist!<br /><br />Kudos, Mr. King, for a wonderful short piece that kept my heart pumping throughout. I will keep finding and devouring these great stories of yours.<br /><br />Love/hate the review? An ever-growing collection of others appears at: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/">http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/</a><br /><br />A Book for All Seasons, a different sort of Book Challenge: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/248185-a-book-for-all-seasons">https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16782390465167417662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2428934267" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2428934267" />
    <a title="Sr3yas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23097409-sr3yas"><img alt="Sr3yas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520526764p2/23097409.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2428934267?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sr3yas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sr3yas" href="/user/show/23097409-sr3yas">Sr3yas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2428934267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11500521948839391109">3.5 Stars<br/><br/><b>One of my friend's Dad used to throw a number of inspirational quotes</b> all around to provide us with insight and direction to life and stuff. One of his favorites was: <i>Don't be afraid to go into the mist, be excited because you don't know where you will end up.</i><br/><br/>Clearly, he never had a chance to read The Mist.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528647900ra/25711368.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>
    <b>❝ In the dream I could hear the rending crack and splinter of breaking trees as God stamped the woods into the shape of His footsteps. He was circling the lake, coming toward </b></blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText11500521948839391109" style="display:none">3.5 Stars<br><br><b>One of my friend's Dad used to throw a number of inspirational quotes</b> all around to provide us with insight and direction to life and stuff. One of his favorites was: <i>Don't be afraid to go into the mist, be excited because you don't know where you will end up.</i><br><br>Clearly, he never had a chance to read The Mist.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528647900ra/25711368.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>
    <b>❝ In the dream I could hear the rending crack and splinter of breaking trees as God stamped the woods into the shape of His footsteps. He was circling the lake, coming toward the Bridgton side, toward us, and all the houses and cottages and summer places were bursting into purple-white flame like lightning, and soon the smoke covered everything. The smoke covered everything like a mist.❞</b>
  </blockquote>
</i><br><br>This dream belongs to David, our narrator/ family man who finds himself living in his own dreadful nightmare. It all began after a destructive storm and when a thick unnatural mist started rolling in. David and his young son Billy were in a crowded supermarket when the mist enveloped the building, effectively creating a prison for the people inside the market, guarded by things no man has ever seen.<br><br><i>How bad is it?</i> Let's just say stepping out to the mist is equivalent to signing your own death sentence. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528647900i/25711369._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Mist is an interesting novella with a very creepy premise. King plays with the horror of the unknown in the opening act and gradually raises the curtain to reveal the main attraction throughout the narration. It's a classic horror structure, and King does it quite well.<br><br>Unfortunately, I had watched the 2007 movie adaptation of the story many times while I was in uni. It was one of gang's favorite movie and we always had conversations which went like: <i>"Dude, remember The Mist's ending? That was crazy".</i> For me, the movie is the reason I'm rating this lower. While The Mist has a "Hitchcock" style ending (Not my words), the movie had a definite one, and in this case, I'll take the definite one.<br><br>Yet, The Mist is the glorious source material and it is really well written. One another thing King nails here is the mob mentality and the way people act under the pressure of horrors. If you're looking for a short SK story, this is the one to pick!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528647900ra/25711370.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Afterthought</b><br><br>For some reason, I kept on thinking a scenario where The Mist finds its way to Derry during the reign of IT. Imagine you're running, and BOOM, IT comes out of the damn smoke.<br><br>That would be a killer tale.</span>

<div id="review_1127800065" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1127800065" />
    <a title="Calista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16731747-calista"><img alt="Calista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436384393p2/16731747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1127800065?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Calista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Calista" href="/user/show/16731747-calista">Calista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">horror fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-drama-tragedy">genre-drama-tragedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=z-stephen-king">z-stephen-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=award-various">award-various</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-short-story">genre-short-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=1980">1980</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1127800065" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9693731985872837611">This is the novella from the short story collection 'Skeleton Crew' by Stephen King. it's one of my favorite stories King has published. He has written some amazing novellas and this is one of my favorites.<br/><br/>I still recall the chills this story gave me. It started out in the woods with a dude cutting wood and I didn't know where it was going and then we end up inside a grocery story with the world going crazy. It's a brilliant story. it has stuck with me for more than 20 years and I still think of</span>
  <span id="freeText9693731985872837611" style="display:none">This is the novella from the short story collection 'Skeleton Crew' by Stephen King. it's one of my favorite stories King has published. He has written some amazing novellas and this is one of my favorites.<br /><br />I still recall the chills this story gave me. It started out in the woods with a dude cutting wood and I didn't know where it was going and then we end up inside a grocery story with the world going crazy. It's a brilliant story. it has stuck with me for more than 20 years and I still think of this story. <br /><br />This story delivers, in my opinion. I use to own all of Stephens books up to 2005, everything. I had a great paperback collection. When I moved I gave them all away and I do wish I still had this story so I could go back and read it again. There are many books in the collection I wish I had kept. Oh well. Hopefully the library opens soon and maybe I can borrow it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9693731985872837611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2102496865" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16699987247436013465"><b>3.5 Misty Stars</b><br/><br/>The Mist was my first read by Stephen King. Well I loved the writing. It keeps you read it uninterrupted. Even though the idea of it wasn’t new, it was something that I watched on movies, but the writing is in such a a way that I couldn’t get enough of it! but I hated its ending! I really didn’t expect the author ends it like that! And by that I meant so open!<br/><br/>The story is about a man, named David, that after a hurricane with his son and his neighbor goes to a supermarket and leave</span>
  <span id="freeText16699987247436013465" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Misty Stars</b><br /><br />The Mist was my first read by Stephen King. Well I loved the writing. It keeps you read it uninterrupted. Even though the idea of it wasn’t new, it was something that I watched on movies, but the writing is in such a a way that I couldn’t get enough of it! but I hated its ending! I really didn’t expect the author ends it like that! And by that I meant so open!<br /><br />The story is about a man, named David, that after a hurricane with his son and his neighbor goes to a supermarket and leaves his wife at home. But when they are at the supermarket, there is a weird fog everywhere. Something is wrong with this fog! Something really creepy and scary!<br /><br />The story is told in David’s POV, 1st person. It’s well-written and fast-paced. It’s a stand-alone novel. All in all, I enjoyed it (except the ending) hope you like it more than me!</span>

<div id="review_1772814146" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1772814146" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1772814146?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8121905-the-mist">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1772814146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5590705199677621627">Starting off this year's October (horror month) with a classic author for when you want to shiver: Stephen King.<br/><br/>I already know the story because I watched the movie adaptation many moons ago so I knew I would like it.<br/>The story is that after a massive storm the titular mist closes in on a community in Maine, but it is no ordinary mist and with it come unspeakable horrors, trapping a number of people in a supermarket.<br/><br/>Stephen King managed to make the supermarket very chilly and claustrophic, giving</span>
  <span id="freeText5590705199677621627" style="display:none">Starting off this year's October (horror month) with a classic author for when you want to shiver: Stephen King.<br /><br />I already know the story because I watched the movie adaptation many moons ago so I knew I would like it.<br />The story is that after a massive storm the titular mist closes in on a community in Maine, but it is no ordinary mist and with it come unspeakable horrors, trapping a number of people in a supermarket.<br /><br />Stephen King managed to make the supermarket very chilly and claustrophic, giving this novella a wonderfully haunting atmosphere. The characters were somewhat authentic. I say somewhat because a certain yellow-clad old lady was almost too over the top (on the other hand, I've seen some American preachers in tents and weird congregations that would be utterly unthinkable here so maybe my European mind just doesn't allow to take it seriously). And as usual, the story is an exploration of the human mind and heart more than it is a story about monsters (unless we call the humans monsters, then we'd be right).<br /><br />What didn't sit right with me at all was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that David had sex with Amanda - I get that they were both emotional and stressed and all, but I will simply not excuse their behaviour (they were both married) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Moreover, much like the author, I think the mind-fuck at the end of the movie was better than the ending of the novella (although this ending wasn't too bad either). It's funny, actually. I would have expected this kind of ending to be typically Hollywood and the movie's ending to be typically King.<br /><br />There were three very powerful realizations in this story, two of which I have already mentioned in my status updates: the horrible things that we imagine can happen to our loved ones, people following even the most bat-shit-insane person if they offer them the solution (no matter how unrealistic) to a bad situation, and finally when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the group arrives at David's driveway only to discover that they cannot get to the house. To have come so far, only to be unable to make it the last few steps so to speak ... being completely helpless after clinging to hope for so long ... having to abandon your partner ... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> - extremely haunting.<br /><br />Anyone looking for an atmospheric and creepy read will get exactly that (plus a character study that drives you up the walls but that is pretty "standard" King ;P).</span>
  <a data-text-id="5590705199677621627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1775701964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17609778883401037997">I saw the movie; I hated the movie. Just now getting to the novella, I'm relieved that it's better and isn't cursed with the horrible celluloid ending.<br/><br/>One of the best perks is I didn't have to listen to as much detaield spiel from that religious woman, who goes down as one of the most annoying characters in horror movie history.<br/><br/>The characters are fine - child is cute and convincing, the MC strong enough although he does distract himself with carnal cravings, and there's the fun disbonding groups</span>
  <span id="freeText17609778883401037997" style="display:none">I saw the movie; I hated the movie. Just now getting to the novella, I'm relieved that it's better and isn't cursed with the horrible celluloid ending.<br /><br />One of the best perks is I didn't have to listen to as much detaield spiel from that religious woman, who goes down as one of the most annoying characters in horror movie history.<br /><br />The characters are fine - child is cute and convincing, the MC strong enough although he does distract himself with carnal cravings, and there's the fun disbonding groups do when they face trouble together.<br /><br />Creepy mist is creepy - there are some nightmarish monsters out there, especially horrible for those like me who detest spiders. As awful as the other creatures were, I'd take them any day over the horrible spiders in this story. *shudder*<br /><br />It flies by pretty quickly, not only because it's a novella but because it's not weighed down with excessive prose. It sticks to the point and sets the creepy ambience well.<br /><br />It's not perfect just because I was only half interested in the storyline (I already knew it going in), but it's a horror novella worth reading, especially this time of the year.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17609778883401037997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer32157583&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer32157583" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2474051801980632099">21W.758 - based on first 20 pages, if I didn't have to read this I'd've already returned it to the freaking library.<br/><br/><b>admittedly only 25% into it:</b><br/>So this is my first King novel. I've read one short story by him which I liked.<br/><br/>Does he <i>always</i> foreshadow with a sledgehammer? And is it <i>him</i> being all snark-snark-me-big-strong-man-protect-small-hot-wife, or is it the narrator? Because I can't tell, but I know I want to punch the narrator any time he says anything about his wife or any other women - it's </span>
  <span id="freeText2474051801980632099" style="display:none">21W.758 - based on first 20 pages, if I didn't have to read this I'd've already returned it to the freaking library.<br /><br /><b>admittedly only 25% into it:</b><br />So this is my first King novel. I've read one short story by him which I liked.<br /><br />Does he <i>always</i> foreshadow with a sledgehammer? And is it <i>him</i> being all snark-snark-me-big-strong-man-protect-small-hot-wife, or is it the narrator? Because I can't tell, but I know I want to punch the narrator any time he says anything about his wife or any other women - it's all got this snobby air of protective superiority, and it's <i>skeeving me out</i>.<br /><br />Also, five-year-olds do not talk like that. Seriously, they don't. Nor does everyone say each other's names in dialogue all the time - they sound like a crowd of news anchors. "I don't know, Norton, let's go to Steff with the weather." Blah.<br /><br /><b>end:</b><br />SO LAME. CLOUD FULL OF DINOSAURS. SO. LAME.<br /><br />So I understand that King is all into the Everyman as Hero thing - characters are easy to relate to (or they're supposed to be; I found it hard to relate to sexist upper-middle-class-white-male artist), their thoughts are all narrated and up-front, narration itself is in plain English, nothing fancy. Except that makes it <i>so boring</i> - plain, bland sentence structure, littered with cliches, utterly toneless.<br /><br />Another apparent trademark is the Juxtaposition of Everyday Details And Anecdotes In Midst Of Horrifying Experience thing - and he flubs it here. We'll be getting up to some monster attack and there is some semblance of tension and then it just <i>flatlines</i> as the narrator pauses to describe the action with some simile that takes three times as many words as it needs to. Or there'll be some emotionally-fraught scene of potential character growth and the narrator will be off and running with some story about his hot wife and the futility of art. And I DID NOT CARE.<br /><br />That was the worst thing about this - King <i>really wanted me to care</i> about these characters, and he kept throwing in details to manipulate me into liking them, and it was <i>so obvious</i>. At the end I was left with Billy, and he was boring, too.<br /><br />I viscerally hated the narrator by page 125 (emphasis mine): "If I were her husband and <b>proprietor</b> of those green eyes and that full figure, I might not travel so much."<br /><br />PROPRIETOR. EXCUSE MY RAGE, BUT WHAT. THE FUCK. IS THAT.<br /><br />At that point, I was like, yeah, whatever, you could totally get eaten right now and I would not even care.<br /><br />So yes: lame-ass plot (THE MIST WAS COMING) with half-assed non-explanation (ARROWHEAD PROJECT. MAYBE) and awful characters (I AM MAN, HEAR ME MAN) that tried to manipulate me into liking them (LOOK I'M HUMAN LOOK HOW HUMAN I AM HERE'S A STORY FROM MY HUMAN LIFE) couched in hideously boring prose.<br /><br />Fail all around, basically. I'll enjoy having a rant about this.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2474051801980632099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3161878870962194792"><b>
  <blockquote> As a species we're fundamentally insane. Put more than two of us in a room, we pick sides and start dreaming up reasons to kill one another. Why do you think we invented politics and religion?</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/813214.The_Mist' title='The Mist by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Mist</a> is a novella mainly about survival and it is a terrifying one at that. For hi</span>
  <span id="freeText3161878870962194792" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote> As a species we're fundamentally insane. Put more than two of us in a room, we pick sides and start dreaming up reasons to kill one another. Why do you think we invented politics and religion?</blockquote>
</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/813214.The_Mist" title="The Mist by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Mist</a> is a novella mainly about survival and it is a terrifying one at that. Because how do one fight off something like the mist and the creatures that came with it?<br /><br />David and his young son Billy happened to be one of a few survivors holing up in a supermarket with more than 80 other people. For his son's sake, David has to decide whether to stay inside (where resources and companions are plentiful) or to go outside (where Death is a high risk) and seek a way to find help. But inside the supermarket, people are starting to get unhinged. They're picking sides, rallying - their survival instincts turning them into something desperate and ferocious. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/813214.The_Mist" title="The Mist by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Mist</a> served as a huge reminder for me. We now walk the grounds in superiority with our civilized minds and manners - top of the food chain. But stripped of all kinds of senses or safety and our primal sides surfaced like a clawing animal. <br /><br />Long short review, this story left me badly shaken inside. It made me question all sorts of What if's. Questions that I never bothered to ask myself. <br /><br />The story ended <i>hopefully </i>- whether David, his son and the others survive to live another day is entirely up to the readers to decide.<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1955250031" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15840085443108587010">“Dreams, after all, are insubstantial things, like mist itself.” <br/>― Stephen King, The Mist<br/><br/><br/>I read The Mist quite awhile ago and also saw the film. Both of them scared the heck out of me and I cannot say this book is one I enjoyed.<br/><br/>I see alot of love for this book on GR and I can see why. Of all the books by King I have read, this one is up there as one of the most genuinely frightening. (And bizarre). <br/><br/>But the books by King that I have loved the most are eerie without being as in your face as The Mi</span>
  <span id="freeText15840085443108587010" style="display:none">“Dreams, after all, are insubstantial things, like mist itself.” <br />― Stephen King, The Mist<br /><br /><br />I read The Mist quite awhile ago and also saw the film. Both of them scared the heck out of me and I cannot say this book is one I enjoyed.<br /><br />I see alot of love for this book on GR and I can see why. Of all the books by King I have read, this one is up there as one of the most genuinely frightening. (And bizarre). <br /><br />But the books by King that I have loved the most are eerie without being as in your face as The Mist is. Now I am not a huge King fan so I do not know all of his books but among my faves are Carrie, Thinner, Needful Things and The Shining.<br /><br />The Mist takes a truly horrifying situation and does put you right there in that claustrophobic supermarket but it is a pretty scary place to be throughout the book. And after awhile the whole thing started getting on my nerves. I guess that is why I am not a fan of Misery either. The setting doesn't change and the scary situations that the characters find themselves in are a constant throughout the book but unlike with some of the books I mentioned that I do like, it is just this one setting for the most part and even though it is suspenseful it wasn't a good suspense for me.<br /><br /> Surprisingly the movie wasn't bungled as most of his books to movies are. (Note: Movie version of Thinner was awful).<br /><br />So for horror purists I do not doubt this was a great read. I like my scares a little more subtle and this was to much for me. 2.5 stars.</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText4554971303908001868" style="display:none">First October Halloween read of the year! I decided to read this book, because it's shorter than a lot of the other Stephen King books. Having many other reads as well, it seemed like a nice read beside the others. <br /><br />The movie of this book is one I haven't seen yet, since I don't watch horror movies since I find them too scary. For some reason I do like to read horror books. Stephen King writes so lively, that I feel completely engrossed into his books when I read them. When you can write a book that makes you scared, you do have an immense gift as a writer. <br /><br />The thought about being stuck in this mist is terrifying. Just the thought makes me shiver, and next time their will be mist where I live I will think completely different about it. The things in the mist sounded terrifying, and truly nightmare material. <br /><br />Still after finishing this book, I have so many questions. What and why? Also, the ending couldn't be more open than this. I can't stand it. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12537970806465481855"><i>The Mist</i> is so much more than just horror. It's a short story and yet, like its fantastic 2007 feature film, it's probably one of the best studies of how humans act when all the little comforts of everyday life are ripped away from them. To quote Ollie from the book, "as a species we're fundamentally insane. Throw us all into a room together and we start picking sides and dreaming up ways to kill one another." Indeed, the biggest threat to David Drayton and his small group of friends trapped in </span>
  <span id="freeText12537970806465481855" style="display:none"><i>The Mist</i> is so much more than just horror. It's a short story and yet, like its fantastic 2007 feature film, it's probably one of the best studies of how humans act when all the little comforts of everyday life are ripped away from them. To quote Ollie from the book, "as a species we're fundamentally insane. Throw us all into a room together and we start picking sides and dreaming up ways to kill one another." Indeed, the biggest threat to David Drayton and his small group of friends trapped in a supermarket is not the violent monsters or the hoards of insects, but instead a religious fanatic, a group of small town rednecks and of course, those who deny that there is even anything in the mist at all.</span>

<div id="review_2733291309" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2733291309" />
    <a title="Celeste" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste"><img alt="Celeste" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481055226p2/7317186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2733291309?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=novella">novella</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2733291309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5171510414908142268"><i>You can find <a href='https://wp.me/pa0WBY-nD' rel='nofollow noopener'>this</a> review and more at <a href='http://novelnotions.net' rel='nofollow noopener'>Novel Notions</a>. </i><br/><br/><i>The Mist</i> is another of King’s works that, like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10592.Carrie' title='Carrie by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carrie</a>, has become such an integral part of society’s collective consciousness regarding fear that it’s become almost cliche. And, as with <i>Carrie</i>, my visit to the Mist completely altered my perception of a story I thought I knew. In my opinion, it went a long towards explaining why King chooses to end stories the way he does, which I’ll get into later. All that being said, <b><i>The Mist</i> is a quick littl</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5171510414908142268" style="display:none"><i>You can find <a href="https://wp.me/pa0WBY-nD" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> review and more at <a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a>. </i><br /><br /><i>The Mist</i> is another of King’s works that, like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10592.Carrie" title="Carrie by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Carrie</a>, has become such an integral part of society’s collective consciousness regarding fear that it’s become almost cliche. And, as with <i>Carrie</i>, my visit to the Mist completely altered my perception of a story I thought I knew. In my opinion, it went a long towards explaining why King chooses to end stories the way he does, which I’ll get into later. All that being said, <b><i>The Mist</i> is a quick little journey into the frightened mind, a dissection of mob mentality and the way fear plays itself out within a group of strangers who are thrown together by sudden and unexplained danger.</b> It’s disturbing and thoughtful and does a fantastic job of putting readers in the shoes of its characters.<br /><br /><b>One thing that King excels at in my opinion is developing believable characters who make believable if unfortunate decisions based on their fear.</b> Our main protagonist and his son find themselves trapped in a supermarket with a bunch of other bystanders, ranging from strangers on holiday to year-round neighbors. In the aftermath of a terrible storm, a strange mist rolls into town. Unfortunately, the mist is much more than the dense fog it appears to be; hidden within the mist are horrid, unearthly creatures that want nothing more than to feed, and humans are evidently pleasing to their palates. Unable to leave the market for fear of being eaten, this motley crew of strangers and neighbors must decide what to do in order to survive.<br /><br /><b>I found it absolutely fascinating to see how group dynamics were fostered and altered by such a large group being trapped together.</b> Little tribes were formed, and leaders of those tribes battled for dominance and greater numbers. We witness a cult develop, led by one of the creepiest human antagonists I’ve witnessed thus far in King’s fiction. We see inhibitions lowered, animal instincts rear their ugly heads, and heroism revealed in the unlikeliest of candidates. We see bravery and cowardice, greed and selflessness, adaptation and blatant closed-mindedness, all writ small within a glass menagerie of a microcosm. <b>I found seeing these big ideas played out on such a small stage incredibly telling of the mixed bag that is humanity. We are capable of such brilliant good, and such mind boggling evil.</b> And all that separates one from the other is the path we choose to follow. Everything always comes back to free will with King’s stories, which rings very true for me.<br /><br /><b>Something I really appreciate about King is his ability to convey belief in something as right and true even in the midst painting religion as horrid and garish.</b> I’ve read around twenty King books, and probably at least a half-dozen of those have featured religious fervor in a negative light. And yet King does a brilliant job of not portraying religious belief itself as evil. Instead, he shows these villains to be fanatics who have twisted religion in some way to suit them. So far, this has always been some twisted form of Christianity, and yet I have never once felt that King was poking fun at Christians. He is instead showing the evil that can be wrought in the name of religion, and how Christianity can become a horribly twisted and dangerous entity when approached from a desire to judge and appear superior instead of a desire for forgiveness and acceptance and love. I have seen my faith twisted in such ways in real life, and it always both saddens and infuriates me. I sense a bit of that in King’s work and it really resonates with me.<br /><br /><b>One thing I particularly appreciated about this book in particular was a nugget near the end of the story that in my opinion explained King’s approach to endings, regarding which he is kind of infamous as they are often ambiguous.</b> <blockquote>“This is what happened. Or, nearly all-there is one final thing I’ll get to in a moment. But you mustn’t expect some neat conclusion…It is, I suppose, what my father always frowningly called “an Alfred Hitchcock ending,” by which he meant a conclusion in ambiguity that allowed the reader or viewer to make up his own mind about how things ended. My father had nothing but contempt for such stories, saying they were ‘cheap shots.’”</blockquote> I really believe this is both an apology and a defense, in a way. King gravitates towards ambiguous endings because they leave things in the hands of readers, but he realizes that this trend of his isn’t always popular. I honestly kind of like ambiguous endings for the very reason King gives us here from the lips of his protagonist. Without a blatant end, readers are free to imagine up their own conclusions, and such stories often live on in our mind longer than their neatly tied counterparts. This is why I think King excels at short stories, because ambiguous endings are for some reason more acceptable when delivered in that format.<br /><br /><i>The Mist</i> is, like most of the books I’ve read from King, not perfect. I can see the flaws, but I was in no way deterred by them. This novella as engrossing as a story set predominantly in a grocery store can hope to be. I just so happened to read the majority of this book on an unusually foggy day, which definitely added on odd ambiance to my reading experience. I also can’t help feeling that novels like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17934530.Annihilation__Southern_Reach___1_" title="Annihilation (Southern Reach, #1) by Jeff VanderMeer" rel="nofollow noopener">Annihilation</a> by Jeff VanderMeer might never have been written if not for this little book. <b><i>The Mist</i> is definitely worth reading, and it a good way of dipping your proverbial toes into King’s scarier stuff.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5171510414908142268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7475151362936698885">I don’t remember when I first read this novel, but it was soon after the hardback version came out at my local library. So I’m guessing 1985 or so.   <span id="freeText7475151362936698885" style="display:none">I don’t remember when I first read this novel, but it was soon after the hardback version came out at my local library. <div id="review_1294919338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1294919338" />
    <a title="Danger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5184971-danger"><img alt="Danger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468949575p2/5184971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1294919338?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danger" href="/user/show/5184971-danger">Danger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1294919338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11654084603246194336">I feel like reading Stephen King is a rite of passage that I somehow completely missed out on. Which is strange. I operate artistically in bizarro fiction, which itself is on the fringes of horror. There are certainly elements of horror in my books to be sure. And with good reason. I love horror movies, horror shows, haunted houses. I spent a good portion of my childhood reading “true story” accounts of ghosts and aliens and wendigos and sasquatches. I obsessed over TV shows like In Search Of… a</span>
  <span id="freeText11654084603246194336" style="display:none">I feel like reading Stephen King is a rite of passage that I somehow completely missed out on. Which is strange. I operate artistically in bizarro fiction, which itself is on the fringes of horror. There are certainly elements of horror in my books to be sure. And with good reason. I love horror movies, horror shows, haunted houses. I spent a good portion of my childhood reading “true story” accounts of ghosts and aliens and wendigos and sasquatches. I obsessed over TV shows like In Search Of… and Unsolved Mysteries. And added to that, I was a voracious reader of just about everything I could get my hands on.<br /><br />But for whatever reason, I never read King. I can't explain why.<br /><br />Now I’m going to judge The Mist a bit harsher than I would, say, one of my friend’s books. Objectively, Stephen King has nothing left to prove and my silly rating isn’t going to help make or break the man’s career. Also, I’ve watched the movie they based off this novella a few times and it’s really one of darkest and most intense films I’ve ever had the pleasure of seeing in a theater. So I was coming in with some expectation.<br /><br />Turns out the film is a pretty decent to the source material, hitting most of the same beats. The movie, however, gets two things right that the book only touches on. The first being Mrs. Carmody’s character (played by Marcia Gay Harden) who in the film is much more prominent as the antagonist. I think it was Harden’s performance that really stole the show in that movie. She was so deplorable and pitch-perfect as a religious zealot that when *SPOILER* her character gets shot in the film, people in the movie theater literally clapped. The second place the film excels over the source material (and this will be apparent to anyone who has seen/read both version of this story) is the ending. The book ends with an ambiguous ending, which is literally referenced in the text itself by the narrator David Drayton. The movie, however, has one of the darkest and devastating endings I can remember. I’ll spare the spoilers for anyone who hasn’t seen, but it’s fucked up.<br /><br />Having only read this one book, it seems to me that Stephen King’s greatest strength as a writer is his almost limitless imagination. I mean, this book turning into a film is not fluke. Almost ALL his books are turned into films.<br /><br />For all his popularity, at least in this book, I imagine his work could’ve benefited from a content editor. Now this is only a 150 page novella and there were still quite a few inane details that added absolutely zero to the actually story. David talking about the lake they live and who lives where and his relationship to them has NOTHING to do with either building David’s character (who is actually kind of dull and douchey) or moving the plot forward. These are cardinal sins for us writer’s at the bottom and it’s one of the first hurdles you need to learn to overcome before anyone starts paying ANY attention to your work. But with King, whose prior success have made him a household name, I feel like content editors were actually AFRAID to touch his work. Think about it. If you were working for Random House and had to edit this VERY FAMOUS writer’s work, are you gonna be like, “Hey, cut the paragraph where you're prattling on about how the main character built some dumb boathouse with his dad”. It ain’t gonna happen. I can only imagine how bad these nonsense details are in some of his longer works which are undoubtedly bloated to fill some sort of expected page count.<br /><br />That said, once the *actual* story gets going, it moves along smoothly and effortlessly. When terrors come sweeping out of the mist, there’s not clunky language or prattling inanity to derail the imagination. I wasn’t TOO surprised by anything that transpired because, as I said, I’ve seen it’s pretty faithful film adaptation, but nevertheless, I was enthralled by all the action/gore sequences. <br /><br />So would I read King again? Absolutely. IN FACT, my copy of The Mist is included in a larger collection of short stories called Skeleton Crew, and I have about 400 more pages to go. And I’m looking forward to reading something I HAVEN’T seen the movie of. Overall, I’d give this 3.5 stars. But since I can’t do that here, I’ll lean towards 4. HAPPY READING, YOU JERKS!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11654084603246194336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_887105910" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/887105910" />
    <a title="Doreen Petersen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24442706-doreen-petersen"><img alt="Doreen Petersen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447577049p2/24442706.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/887105910?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Doreen Petersen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Doreen Petersen" href="/user/show/24442706-doreen-petersen">Doreen Petersen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer887105910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13171574265812269834">A fascinating and tormenting tale. What caused the mist? What was it made of? Did the 4 people who made it out of the supermarket survive? There are no answers to these questions which might possibly leave an opening for a sequel?</span>

<div id="review_1085940939" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1085940939" />
    <a title="ᴥ Irena ᴥ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5252054-irena"><img alt="ᴥ Irena ᴥ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425497470p2/5252054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1085940939?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ᴥ Irena ᴥ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ᴥ Irena ᴥ" href="/user/show/5252054-irena">ᴥ Irena ᴥ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8121905-the-mist">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5252054-irena?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1085940939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17894271456128648809"><i>The Mist</i> is a great monster story. The whole plot mostly takes place inside the supermarket (at least the largest horror one). After a nasty storm a strange mist appears. And the things in it.<br/>People escaped the mist and what is lurking in it and now they either have to wait for it to pass or to do something horrible. It isn't surprising, then, that you get a couple of stereotypical characters (an old crazy doom-sayer, a lawyer who is full of himself, a unassuming good guy and so on). The protago</span>
  <span id="freeText17894271456128648809" style="display:none"><i>The Mist</i> is a great monster story. The whole plot mostly takes place inside the supermarket (at least the largest horror one). After a nasty storm a strange mist appears. And the things in it.<br />People escaped the mist and what is lurking in it and now they either have to wait for it to pass or to do something horrible. It isn't surprising, then, that you get a couple of stereotypical characters (an old crazy doom-sayer, a lawyer who is full of himself, a unassuming good guy and so on). The protagonist is stuck with his five-year-old son there.<br /><br />As I said, it is a great monster story. I really liked that part. Unfortunately, in a story like this I need to root for the main character or at least to accept his actions on some level. That definitely doesn't happen here. I loved the story up to a particular moment that was completely unnecessary. It didn't move the story forward. All it did was to make me lose my interest. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17894271456128648809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('o5YsaaiC9MFQo7aIw2/2gBKr71SP4g7UIh9uOlSkEwK+EZcIRFKx5PWwZVfp28SaFVybD41B17Dddhk5mRb+ow==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uecIivshYtSZoS9vNiCKq0wq8X0Ne/29rQx5E887CjOkYLPrF/En8Tyy/LAclLixS92FJg/YJNlSZQ4QAonnkg==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">About Stephen King</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1362814142p3/3389.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">Stephen King
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer371433797882719097">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, M</span>
  <span id="freeText371433797882719097" style="display:none">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, Maine, for good. Her parents, Guy and Nellie Pillsbury, had become incapacitated with old age, and Ruth King was persuaded by her sisters to take over the physical care of them. Other family members provided a small house in Durham and financial support. After Stephen's grandparents passed away, Mrs. King found work in the kitchens of Pineland, a nearby residential facility for the mentally challenged.<br /><br />Stephen attended the grammar school in Durham and Lisbon Falls High School, graduating in 1966. From his sophomore year at the University of Maine at Orono, he wrote a weekly column for the school newspaper, THE MAINE CAMPUS. He was also active in student politics, serving as a member of the Student Senate. He came to support the anti-war movement on the Orono campus, arriving at his stance from a conservative view that the war in Vietnam was unconstitutional. He graduated in 1970, with a B.A. in English and qualified to teach on the high school level. A draft board examination immediately post-graduation found him 4-F on grounds of high blood pressure, limited vision, flat feet, and punctured eardrums.<br /><br />He met Tabitha Spruce in the stacks of the Fogler Library at the University, where they both worked as students; they married in January of 1971. As Stephen was unable to find placement as a teacher immediately, the Kings lived on his earnings as a laborer at an industrial laundry, and her student loan and savings, with an occasional boost from a short story sale to men's magazines.<br /><br />Stephen made his first professional short story sale ("The Glass Floor") to <i>Startling Mystery Stories</i> in 1967. Throughout the early years of his marriage, he continued to sell stories to men's magazines. Many were gathered into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10628.Night_Shift" title="Night Shift" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Shift</a> collection or appeared in other anthologies.<br /><br />In the fall of 1971, Stephen began teaching English at Hampden Academy, the public high school in Hampden, Maine. Writing in the evenings and on the weekends, he continued to produce short stories and to work on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="371433797882719097" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
